Conditions for a Valid Confession of Zina
Lists conditions for a valid confession of zina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid confession of zina in Hanafi law and identify which conditions, if violated, invalidate the confession.

Core Idea
A valid confession of zina must be explicit, sober, and free from contradiction or physical impossibility.

Confession (iqrar) is a powerful proof in Islamic law, but in hudud cases, the Hanafi school imposes strict conditions to avoid false confessions. This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya outlines the essential conditions for a confession of zina to be legally valid. Each condition serves to eliminate doubt (shubha) and uphold the principle that hudud are averted by doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The passage discusses the confession (iqrar) of zina. Recognise that confession is a substitute for eyewitness testimony.
2
List the conditions
Extract the conditions: (1) explicit wording, (2) sobriety, (3) no denial by the other party, (4) no physical impossibility (intact organ for man, no ratq for woman), (5) neither party mute.
3
Understand the rationale
Each condition is designed to remove doubts. For example, intoxication may lead to false confession; muteness may hide a valid reason to drop hadd.
Shubha (doubt) is the key principle.
4
Note the exception
If the confession is invalid due to intoxication, but the act was witnessed by two or more witnesses, hadd is still imposed because the certainty of witnesses overrides the doubt from confession.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test your understanding by applying the conditions to a hypothetical case, such as a drunk confession without witnesses.
The confession is rejected and no hadd is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ اس باب سے متعلق چند ضروری مسائل یہاں بیان کئے جاتے ہیں۔ وہ اپنے اپنے موقع سے متعلق کئے جائیں۔ زنا کا اقرار ثابت ہوتا ہے مگر شرط یہ ہے کہ اقرار صراحت کے ساتھ ہو۔ اور اقرار کے وقت نشہ کی حالت میں نہ ہو۔ اور مرد و عورت میں سے کوئی بھی دوسرے کو جھٹلاتا نہ ہو۔ یا اس کا جھوٹا ہونا ظاہر نہ ہو۔ اس طرح سے کہ مرد کا آلہ تناسل کٹا ہوا ہونا ثابت ہو۔ یا عورت کو رتق کی بیماری ہو یعنی پیشاب گاہ کے اوپر کی ہڈیاں اس طرح سے ملی ہوئی ہوں کہ ان کے درمیان آلہ داخل نہ ہو سکے۔ جس عورت کے ساتھ زنا کا اقرارو دعویٰ کیا ہو یا اس کے برعکس عورت نے جس مرد کے ساتھ زنا کا دعویٰ کیا ہو ان میں سے کوئی بھی گونگا نہ ہو اس احتمال کی بناء پر کہ اس میں ایسی بات رہ گئی ہو جو زبان سے ظاہر نہیں کی جاسکتی ہو مگر اس کی وجہ سے حد ساقط ہو جاتی ہو اور اگر نشہ کی حالت میں زنایا چوری کا اقرار کیا ہو تو اس پر حد جاری نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ شاید اس نے جھوٹا اقرار کیا ہو۔ البتہ اگر گواہوں کے سامنے زنا کیا یا چوری کی تو حد ماری جائے گی۔
Benefit: Some necessary issues related to this chapter are mentioned here. They should be related to their appropriate places. Confession of zina is established, but the condition is that the confession be explicit. And at the time of confession, not be in a state of intoxication. And neither the man nor the woman should deny the other. Or its falsehood should not become apparent, such that it is established that the man's penis is cut off, or the woman has the disease of ratq (vaginal atresia), meaning the bones above the urethra are fused such that no organ can enter between them. The woman with whom zina is confessed or claimed, or vice versa, neither of them should be mute, on the possibility that there may be something left unsaid that cannot be expressed verbally but due to which the hadd is dropped. And if a confession of zina or theft is made in a state of intoxication, hadd will not be executed because he might have made a false confession. However, if he committed zina or theft in front of witnesses, hadd will be imposed.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing the conditions for a valid confession of zina. The Hanafi school holds that for a confession to be legally effective, it must be explicit (clear and unambiguous). The confessor must be sober; a confession made while intoxicated is invalid because it may be false. Both the man and woman must confirm the act; if either denies, the confession is not accepted. Additionally, if physical impossibility is established (e.g., the man is castrated or the woman has ratq, a condition preventing intercourse), the confession is rejected. Neither party should be mute, because a mute person might have reasons that cannot be expressed, which could drop the hadd. If a confession is made while drunk, it is not acted upon; but if the crime was witnessed by two or more witnesses, then the hadd is imposed regardless of confession. This ruling is based on the principle that in hudud punishments, doubts (shubha) are to be avoided, and a confession under intoxication raises doubt.

Key Terms
رتق (ratq): A medical condition where the vaginal passage is blocked or fused.
اقرار (iqrar): A voluntary confession or admission of a crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is accepted and hadd is imposed.
B) It is accepted only if the person is a repeat offender.
C) It is not accepted and hadd is not imposed.
D) It is accepted but with a lighter penalty.

Key Takeaway
A valid confession of zina must be explicit, sober, not contradicted, not physically impossible, and from a non-mute; otherwise, hadd is not applied without witnesses.

Retraction from Confession in Hudud: Scope and Exceptions
Rulings on retraction from confession in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on retraction from confession in hudud and apply the principle to determine when retraction is accepted.

Core Idea
Retraction from confession in hudud is valid for purely Allah's rights, reflecting the Hanafi emphasis on doubt and mercy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a series of rulings on retraction from confession in hudud cases. The Hanafi school consistently allows retraction, recognizing that doubt (shubha) can invalidate the basis for punishment. The text also addresses related scenarios such as harm inflicted on the condemned before execution and the case of a sick person. Understanding these rulings clarifies the Hanafi approach to criminal penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on retraction
The text states that if a confessor retracts, flees, or denies, it is considered a valid retraction. This is the starting point for all hudud based on confession.
This applies to hudud proven by confession only.
2
Determine the scope of retraction: pure Allah's rights
Retraction is accepted in hudud that are purely Allah's rights, such as drinking alcohol and theft. This excludes hudud involving rights of individuals (e.g., qadhf).
The basis is the hadd for qadhf involves a right of the victim.
3
Examine the ruling on retraction of ihsan confession
If a person confesses to being muhsan (a condition for stoning) and then retracts, the retraction is accepted. This shows the principle applies to all conditions related to the hadd.
Ihsan is a condition for rajm, not a hadd itself.
4
Consider ancillary scenarios: harm inflicted on the condemned
If someone harms the condemned after the rajm order, no qisas or diyah; before the order, qisas or diyah applies. This shows that after the order, the person is deemed to have forfeited his inviolability.
This ruling is based on the principle that the condemned's life is no longer protected by the shari'ah.
5
Apply the ruling to a sick person
If lashes are obligatory and the sick person has no hope of recovery, the lashes are administered without delay. This avoids the punishment being entirely wasted.
This is a practical application of the principle that hudud should be executed when possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۔ اگر اقرار کرنے والے مجرم نے اپنے اقرار سے رجوع کیا یا حد لگائی جانے کے وقت بھاگ گیا۔ یا اقرار سے انکار کیا تو اسے دعوئی سے رجوع کر لینا سمجھا جائے گا۔ جیسے مرتد ہونے سے انکار کرنا ہے۔ ۵۔ اگر اپنے محصن ہونے کا پہلے اقرار کیا پھر اس سے رجوع کر لیا تو انکار صحیح ہوگا۔ - ۔ اسی طرح وہ حدود جو حقوق العباد میں سے نہ ہوں بلکہ محض حقوق اللہ میں سے ہوں جیسے شرابخوری کی حد اور چوری کی حد میں اگر اقرار سے ان کا ثبوت ہو پھر وہ اپنے اقرار سے پھر جائے تو صحیح ہے۔ ے۔ اگر کسی شخص کے رجم کرنے کا حکم دیدیا گیا پھر رجم کرنے سے پہلے کسی نے قید خانہ میں جا کر اس کی ایک آنکھ پھوڑ دی یا اسے قتل کر دیا تو اس پر نہ تو قصاص لازم ہوگا اور نہ اس کا کچھ عوض لازم آئے گا اور اگر رجم کا حکم ہونے سے پہلے اس نے ایسا کیا۔ اب اگر اس نے ایسا قصداً کیا ہو تو قصاص واجب ہوگا اور اگر خطاء ہوا ہو تو دیت واجب ہوگی۔ - اگر مریض پر درے واجب ہوں لیکن پہلے سے ہی اس کی صحت سے مایوس ہو چکی ہوتو صحت کا انتظام کئے بغیرہی اسے درے مارے جائیں۔(البحر )
If the criminal who confessed retracts his confession, or runs away at the time of execution of hadd, or denies the confession, it will be considered as retraction from the claim, just like denying apostasy. 5. If he first confessed his ihsan (being muhsan) and then retracted, the denial is valid. Similarly, the hudud that are not among the rights of the slaves but are purely the rights of Allah, such as the hadd for drinking alcohol and the hadd for theft, if they are proven by confession and then he retracts, it is valid. And if a person was ordered to be stoned (rajm), and before the stoning someone went to the prison and gouged out his eye or killed him, then there is no qisas upon him nor any compensation. But if it was done before the order of rajm, then if he did it intentionally, qisas is obligatory; if by mistake, diyah is obligatory. And if lashes are obligatory upon a sick person, but his recovery has already been despaired of, then the lashes will be applied without arranging for his health. (al-Bahr)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement covering several sub-rulings related to hadd. First, retraction from a confession is accepted. If a confessor denies his confession or flees before execution, it is treated as retraction. Second, if someone confesses to being muhsan (which is a condition for stoning) and then retracts, the retraction is accepted. Third, for hudud that are purely Allah's rights (like drinking alcohol and theft), retraction after confession is also accepted. This is because the right of Allah is based on mercy and the door is left open for repentance. Fourth, if someone harms the condemned person before rajm, there is no qisas if the order for rajm has been given; before the order, qisas or diyah applies. Fifth, for a sick person with no hope of recovery, lashes are administered immediately without waiting for health. These rulings demonstrate the legal framework for hadd execution and the acceptance of doubt (shubha) that arises from retraction.

Key Terms
احصان (ihsan): The status of being muhsan: free, adult, Muslim, married, and having consummated the marriage.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction or withdrawal of a legal claim or confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person confesses to drinking alcohol and then retracts before hadd is executed?
A) The retraction is ignored and hadd is applied.
B) The retraction is accepted and hadd is not applied.
C) He must provide a reason for retraction.
D) He is given a lighter penalty.

Key Takeaway
Retraction from confession in hudud is accepted for purely Allah's rights, reflecting the Hanafi principle that doubt (shubha) averts punishment.

Conditions of Ihsan for Rajm
Defines conditions for ihsan in rajm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for ihsan for rajm and explain the legal effect of apostasy and divorce on ihsan.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires freedom, Islam, adulthood, and a valid consummated marriage — once attained, it is never lost.

The hadd of rajm is the severest punishment for zina, reserved for those who have attained the status of muhsan. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya enumerates the precise conditions that constitute ihsan according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the law of hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of ihsan
Ihsan is a condition for rajm; without it, the penalty for zina is 100 lashes. Determine what legal status the offender must have to be eligible for stoning.
Rajm is only for muhsan offenders.
2
List the explicit conditions
From the text, extract the five requirements: being free, Muslim, adult, having a valid marriage with consummation, and both spouses being muhsan at the time of consummation.
The fifth condition is specific to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Note exceptions and clarifications
The text addresses defective marriages: if a fasid marriage becomes valid before consummation, it suffices. Also, apostasy does not nullify ihsan, and the marriage need not continue.
These nuances prevent common misunderstandings.
4
Apply to a hypothetical
Consider a free, adult Muslim who was validly married and consummated, then divorced. He commits zina. Apply the conditions: he remains muhsan, so rajm applies.
Divorce does not remove ihsan.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Some schools do not require both spouses to be muhsan. The Hanafi position is stricter, requiring both to be free and Muslim at consummation.
This may affect the ruling in mixed-faith marriages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجم کرنے کے لئے جو احصان کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ اس کے لئے چند باتوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ آزاد ہونا۔ ا۔ ۴۔ مسلمان ہونا۔ ۵۔ کسی محصنہ عورت کے اقل ہونا۔ ۳۔ بالغ ہونا۔ ساتھ نکاح صحیح کر کے دخول کا بھی ہونا۔ اب اگر پہلے نکاح فاسد کیا ہو لیکن دخول سے پہلے صحیح ہو گیا ہو تو بھی صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ - ولی کے وقت خود بھی اور اس کی بیوی بھی یعنی دونوں ہی میں احصان کی صفت پائی جارہی ہو۔ - مرتد ہو جانے سے اس کا احصان باطل نہ ہو۔ نوف حصان باقی رنے کے لئے کام کا باقی رہنا ر نہیںہے۔ چا چار عر ب میں اک باری کا کیا پھر سے طلاق دے کر تنہائیکی نکاح کیا: زندگی بسر کرتے ہوئے کسی عورت سے زنا کر لیا تو بھی اس پر حد جاری کی جائے گی۔
For stoning, the condition of ihsan is required. For this, several things are necessary: being free, being Muslim, being an adult, and having a valid marriage with consummation. Now, if he first had a defective (fasid) marriage but it became valid before consummation, it is valid. At the time of consummation, both he and his wife should possess the attribute of ihsan. Apostasy does not nullify his ihsan. For the continuation of ihsan, it is not necessary that the marriage continue. ... If he committed zina with a woman while living his life, hadd will be executed on him.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for ihsan required for the hadd of rajm (stoning). The Hanafi school requires five conditions: the offender must be free, Muslim, adult, married (to a woman who is also muhsana), and the marriage must have been valid and consummated. If a marriage was initially defective but became valid before consummation, it suffices. Both spouses must be muhsan at the time of consummation. Apostasy does not break ihsan; the condition of ihsan once attained remains even if the marriage ends. The last part appears to state that if a muhsan person commits zina, hadd is applied.

Key Terms
احصان (ihsan): The legal status of being muhsan: free, adult, Muslim, married with consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for ihsan for rajm according to the text?
A) Being free.
B) Being a Muslim.
C) Being a virgin.
D) Being in a valid marriage with consummation.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan for rajm requires five conditions; once attained, it remains even after divorce or apostasy.
